# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

52-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive mapping of the Grafana unified alerting (ngalert) subsystem. Here's what I've documented:

## Summary

The answer file includes:

### **Five Core Components** (as requested):

1. **Alert Rule Storage** (`pkg/services/ngalert/store/`)
   - `DBstore` manages alert rules, Alertmanager config, and alert instances
   - Dual instance storage backends (JSON and Protobuf)

2. **Scheduler** (`pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/`)
   - `ScheduleService` orchestrates rule evaluation timing
   - Registry-based rule tracking with retry logic
   - Support for both alert rules and recording rules

3. **State Manager** (`pkg/services/ngalert/state/`)
   - `Manager` tracks alert state in-memory with caching
   - Multiple persistence strategies (sync/async at instance or rule-group level)
   - State transitions from normal → alerting → pending

4. **Notifier** (`pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/`)
   - `MultiOrgAlertmanager` manages per-organization Alertmanager instances
   - Supports local, remote-primary, and remote-secondary modes
   - Configuration and receiver management

5. **History Writer** (`pkg/services/ngalert/state/historian/` + `pkg/services/ngalert/writer/`)
   - Multiple backends: annotations, Loki, Prometheus, multi-backend
   - Records state transitions for audit trails and dashboards
   - Smart filtering (only records meaningful transitions)

### **Additional Components Documented**:

- **Evaluation Engine** (`eval/`) - Executes alert rule queries
- **Alerts Router** (`sender/`) - Routes evaluated alerts to Alertmanager
- **Service Orchestrator** (`ngalert.go`) - Coordinates all components

The file includes 46 key Go source files, 17 major symbols, and a detailed narrative explaining the architecture, data flow, and key interfaces.

if full path to the folder is changed, we update all alert rules in that folder to make sure that all peers (in HA mode) will update folder title and\n605: \t// clean up the current state\n606: \tbus.AddEventListener(func(ctx context.Context, evt *events.FolderFullPathUpdated) error {\n607: \t\tlogger.Info(\"Got folder full path updated event. updating rules in the folders\", \"folderUIDs\", evt.UIDs)\n608: \n609: \t\t// Increment version for all rules\n610: \t\tupdatedKeys, err := dbStore.IncreaseVersionForAllRulesInNamespaces(ctx, evt.OrgID, evt.UIDs)\n611: \t\tif err != nil {\n612: \t\t\tlogger.Error(\"Failed to update alert rules in the folders after their full paths were changed\", \"error\", err, \"folderUIDs\", evt.UIDs, \"orgID\", evt.OrgID)\n613: \t\t\treturn err\n614: \t\t}\n615: \t\tlogger.Info(\"Updated version for alert rules\", \"keys\", updatedKeys)\n616: \n617: \t\t// Update folder fullpaths for all rules\n618: \t\tif err := dbStore.UpdateFolderFullpathsForFolders(ctx, evt.OrgID, evt.UIDs); err != nil {\n619: \t\t\tlogger.Error(\"Failed to update folder fullpaths for alert rules\", \"error\", err, \"folderUIDs\", evt.UIDs, \"orgID\", evt.OrgID)\n620: \t\t\treturn err\n621: \t\t}\n622: \t\tlogger.Info(\"Updated folder fullpaths for alert rules\", \"folderUIDs\", evt.UIDs)\n623: \n624: \t\treturn nil\n625: \t})\n626: }\n627: \n628: // BackfillFolderFullpaths populates folder_fullpath for all existing alert rules.\n629: // This is a one-time operation that runs during startup after the migration.\n630: func (ng *AlertNG) BackfillFolderFullpaths(ctx context.Context) error {\n631: \t// Get all organizations\n632: \torgIDs, err := ng.store.FetchOrgIds(ctx)\n633: \tif err != nil {\n634: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to fetch organizations: %w\", err)\n635: \t}\n636: \n637: \tanyBackfilled := false\n638: \tfor _, orgID := range orgIDs {\n639: \t\tselect {\n640: \t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n641: \t\t\treturn ctx.Err()\n642: \t\tdefault:\n643: \t\t}\n644: \n645: \t\t// Get all unique folder UIDs for this org from alert_rule table where folder_fullpath is NULL\n646: \t\tvar folderUIDs []string\n647: \t\terr := ng.SQLStore.WithDbSession(ctx, func(sess *db.Session) error {\n648: \t\t\treturn sess.SQL(`\n649: \t\t\t\tSELECT DISTINCT namespace_uid\n650: \t\t\t\tFROM alert_rule\n651: \t\t\t\tWHERE org_id = ? AND folder_fullpath IS NULL\n652: \t\t\t`, orgID).Find(&folderUIDs)\n653: \t\t})\n654: \t\tif err != nil {\n655: \t\t\tng.Log.Error(\"Failed to fetch folder UIDs for backfill\", \"org_id\", orgID, \"error\", err)\n656: \t\t\tcontinue\n657: \t\t}\n658: \n659: \t\tif len(folderUIDs) == 0 {\n660: \t\t\tcontinue\n661: \t\t}\n662: \n663: \t\tif !anyBackfilled {\n664: \t\t\tng.Log.Info(\"Starting backfill of folder fullpaths for alert rules\")\n665: \t\t\tanyBackfilled = true\n666: \t\t}\n667: \n668: \t\tng.Log.Info(\"Backfilling folder fullpaths\", \"org_id\", orgID, \"folder_count\", len(folderUIDs))\n669: \n670: \t\t// Use the existing sync method to populate fullpaths\n671: \t\tif err := ng.store.UpdateFolderFullpathsForFolders(ctx, orgID, folderUIDs); Grafana unified alerting subsystem is implemented in `pkg/services/ngalert/` and consists of several interconnected major components:\\n\\n## 1. Service Orchestrator (`ngalert.go`)\\n\\nThe main entry point is `AlertNG` in `pkg/services/ngalert/ngalert.go`. The `ProvideService()` function initializes all components and `AlertNG.Run()` orchestrates their execution. The architecture follows a typical pipeline:\\n\\n1. **Alert Rule Storage** receives rules from the database\\n2. **Scheduler** fetches rules and determines evaluation timing\\n3. **Evaluator** executes rule queries against data sources\\n4. **State Manager** tracks alert state transitions\\n5. **History Writer** persists state changes for audit/dashboards\\n6. **Notifier** sends alerts through Alertmanager\\n7. **Alerts Router** dispatches to external Alertmanagers\\n\\n## 2. Alert Rule Storage (`store/`)\\n\\nThe storage layer is implemented by `DBstore` in `pkg/services/ngalert/store/database.go`. This component manages:\\n\\n- **Alert Rules**: `store/alert_rule.go` - CRUD operations for alert rules\\n- **Alertmanager Config**: `store/alertmanager.go` - Configuration storage and versioning\\n- **Alert Instances**: Two backends for storing alert instance state:\\n  - `store/instance_database.go` - Simple JSON-based instance storage\\n  - `store/proto_instance_database.go` - Protobuf-compressed instance storage (feature flag controlled)\\n\\nThe `DBstore` implements interfaces like `AlertingStore`, `RuleStore`, and `InstanceStore` that other components depend on.\\n\\n## 3. Scheduler (`schedule/`)\\n\\nThe scheduler is implemented in `pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/schedule.go`. It contains:\\n\\n- **ScheduleService Interface**: Defines the scheduling contract\\n- **Rule Registry**: `schedule/registry.go` maintains loaded alert rules\\n- **Alert Rule Scheduling**: `schedule/alert_rule.go` handles alert rule evaluation scheduling\\n- **Recording Rule Scheduling**: `schedule/recording_rule.go` manages Prometheus recording rules\\n- **Rule Fetcher**: `schedule/fetcher.go` loads rules from the database\\n\\nThe scheduler uses a base interval tick system to evaluate rules at their configured intervals. It manages retry logic with exponential backoff for failed evaluations.\\n\\n## 4. State Manager (`state/`)\\n\\nThe state management subsystem is core to ngalert and implemented in `pkg/services/ngalert/state/manager.go`. Key components:\\n\\n- **Manager**: Central coordinator that tracks alert state in memory\\n- **State Transitions**: `state/state.go` defines state machines and transitions (normal, alerting, pending, no data)\\n- **State Cache**: `state/cache.go` holds in-memory alert state for fast access\\n- **State Persistence**: Multiple persister implementations:\\n  - `state/persister_sync.go` - Synchronous write to database\\n  - `state/persister_sync_rule.go` - Sync at rule group level\\n  - `state/persister_async.go` - Asynchronous batched writes\\n  - `state/persister_async_rule.go` - Async at rule group level\\n- **Instance Store Interface**: Multiple implementations for reading/writing instance state\\n  - `state/multi_instance_reader.go` - Reads from multiple backends during feature flag transitions\\n  - `state/store_state_reader.go` - Reads state from database (for HA mode)\\n\\n## 5. History Writer (`state/historian/` and `writer/`)\\n\\nThe history writer subsystem records all alert state transitions for audit trails and panel annotations. Implemented in:\\n\\n- **Historian Core**: `state/historian/core.go` - Logic for determining which transitions to record\\n  - `ShouldRecord()` - Decides if a transition should be written to history\\n  - `ShouldRecordAnnotation()` - Decides if dashboard annotations should be created\\n  - Label fingerprinting for stable alert identification\\n\\n- **Backend Abstraction**: `state/historian/backend.go` defines `BackendType`:\\n  - `annotations` - Stores in Grafana dashboard annotations\\n  - `loki` - Remote Loki for long-term retention\\n  - `prometheus` - Remote Prometheus for metrics\\n  - `multiple` - Hybrid multi-backend setup\\n  - `noop` - Disabled\\n\\n- **Backend Implementations**:\\n  - `state/historian/annotation.go` / `annotation_store.go` - Grafana annotations backend\\n  - `state/historian/loki.go` - Remote Loki backend\\n  - `state/historian/prometheus.go` - Remote Prometheus backend\\n  - `state/historian/multiple.go` - Multi-backend coordinator\\n\\n- **Remote Writer**: `writer/datasourcewriter.go` - Generic datasource writer for remote backends\\n\\n## 6. Notifier/Alertmanager (`notifier/`)\\n\\nThe notification subsystem manages alert routing and notification delivery:\\n\\n- **MultiOrgAlertmanager**: `notifier/multiorg_alertmanager.go` - Multi-tenant wrapper\\n  - Manages per-organization Alertmanager instances\\n  - Handles configuration loading and synchronization\\n  - Manages clustering peers for HA deployments\\n  - Remote primary/secondary modes for delegated alertmanaging\\n\\n- **Alertmanager Interface**: `notifier/alertmanager.go` defines core operations:\\n  - Config management (apply, save, retrieve)\\n  - Silence operations (create, delete, list)\\n  - Alert operations (get, put)\\n  - Receiver management\\n  - Status tracking\\n\\n- **Configuration**: `notifier/alertmanager_config.go` - Alertmanager configuration handling\\n- **Auto-generation**: `notifier/autogen_alertmanager.go` - Default config generation\\n- **Receivers**: `notifier/receiver_svc.go` - Receiver CRUD operations\\n- **Silences**: `notifier/silence_svc.go` - Silence management\\n- **Sender**: `notifier/sender.go` - Alert sending to Alertmanager\\n\\n## 7. Alerts Router/Sender (`sender/`)\\n\\nResponsible for routing evaluated alerts to the Alertmanager:\\n\\n- **AlertsRouter**: `sender/router.go` - Main router that syncs config and routes alerts\\n  - Loads Alertmanager configuration from database\\n  - Applies configuration to Alertmanager instances\\n  - Periodically polls configuration for changes\\n  - Dispatches alerts to appropriate Alertmanager\\n\\n- **External Alertmanager Sender**: `sender/sender.go` - Sends alerts to external Alertmanagers\\n  - Queue-based alert batching\\n  - HTTP client management\\n  - Retry and backoff logic\\n\\n- **Notifier**: `sender/notifier.go` - Adapts alerts for Alertmanager format\\n\\n## 8. Evaluation (`eval/`)\\n\\nRule evaluation engine in `pkg/services/ngalert/eval/`:\\n\\n- **Evaluator**: `eval/eval.go` - Executes alert rule queries\\n  - Supports queries against Prometheus-compatible datasources\\n  - Supports Grafana expressions (math, reduce, etc.)\\n  - Returns numeric values with labels\\n  - Handles no-data and error conditions\\n\\n- **EvaluatorFactory**: Creates evaluators with proper dependencies\\n- **Validation**: `eval/validate.go` - Validates rule conditions before execution\\n- **Context**: `eval/context.go` - Execution context for evaluations\\n\\n## 9. Evaluation Runner\\n\\nThe `evaluationRunner` in `evaluation_runner.go` coordinates the evaluation pipeline:\\n\\n- Spawns goroutines for each rule evaluation\\n- Calls the scheduler to get rules\\n- Invokes evaluators\\n- Passes results to state manager\\n- Handles lifecycle (startup, shutdown)\\n\\n## Data Flow\\n\\n1. **Startup**: `ngalert.go:init()` initializes all components, warming up state cache from database\\n2. **Scheduling**: Scheduler fetches rules from store and builds evaluation schedule\\n3. **Evaluation**: EvaluationRunner triggers rule evaluations at scheduled intervals\\n4. **State Management**: Evaluator results flow to State Manager which:\\n   - Compares against previous state\\n   - Generates StateTransition objects\\n   - Calls StatePersister to save state\\n   - Calls Historian to record changes\\n5. **Notification**: State transitions are sent to AlertsRouter which:\\n   - Formats alerts\\n   - Routes to Alertmanager\\n   - Alertmanager applies routing and sending rules\\n6. **Persistence**: History Writer backends persist state transitions for audit/dashboards\\n\\n## Key Interfaces\\n\\n- `AlertingStore` / `RuleStore` - Store layer contracts\\n- `ScheduleService` - Scheduler contract\\n- `AlertInstanceManager` - State access\\n- `Historian` - History writing\\n- `Alertmanager` - Notification interface\\n- `StatePersister` - State persistence\\n- `EvaluatorFactory` - Rule evaluation\\n\\nThis architecture enables Grafana to evaluate alert rules at scale with support for HA deployments, multiple notification backends, and comprehensive state history tracking.\"\n}\n",

Grafana unified alerting subsystem is implemented in `pkg/services/ngalert/` and consists of several interconnected major components:\\n\\n## 1. Service Orchestrator (`ngalert.go`)\\n\\nThe main entry point is `AlertNG` in `pkg/services/ngalert/ngalert.go`. The `ProvideService()` function initializes all components and `AlertNG.Run()` orchestrates their execution. The architecture follows a typical pipeline:\\n\\n1. **Alert Rule Storage** receives rules from the database\\n2. **Scheduler** fetches rules and determines evaluation timing\\n3. **Evaluator** executes rule queries against data sources\\n4. **State Manager** tracks alert state transitions\\n5. **History Writer** persists state changes for audit/dashboards\\n6. **Notifier** sends alerts through Alertmanager\\n7. **Alerts Router** dispatches to external Alertmanagers\\n\\n## 2. Alert Rule Storage (`store/`)\\n\\nThe storage layer is implemented by `DBstore` in `pkg/services/ngalert/store/database.go`. This component manages:\\n\\n- **Alert Rules**: `store/alert_rule.go` - CRUD operations for alert rules\\n- **Alertmanager Config**: `store/alertmanager.go` - Configuration storage and versioning\\n- **Alert Instances**: Two backends for storing alert instance state:\\n  - `store/instance_database.go` - Simple JSON-based instance storage\\n  - `store/proto_instance_database.go` - Protobuf-compressed instance storage (feature flag controlled)\\n\\nThe `DBstore` implements interfaces like `AlertingStore`, `RuleStore`, and `InstanceStore` that other components depend on.\\n\\n## 3. Scheduler (`schedule/`)\\n\\nThe scheduler is implemented in `pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/schedule.go`. It contains:\\n\\n- **ScheduleService Interface**: Defines the scheduling contract\\n- **Rule Registry**: `schedule/registry.go` maintains loaded alert rules\\n- **Alert Rule Scheduling**: `schedule/alert_rule.go` handles alert rule evaluation scheduling\\n- **Recording Rule Scheduling**: `schedule/recording_rule.go` manages Prometheus recording rules\\n- **Rule Fetcher**: `schedule/fetcher.go` loads rules from the database\\n\\nThe scheduler uses a base interval tick system to evaluate rules at their configured intervals. It manages retry logic with exponential backoff for failed evaluations.\\n\\n## 4. State Manager (`state/`)\\n\\nThe state management subsystem is core to ngalert and implemented in `pkg/services/ngalert/state/manager.go`. Key components:\\n\\n- **Manager**: Central coordinator that tracks alert state in memory\\n- **State Transitions**: `state/state.go` defines state machines and transitions (normal, alerting, pending, no data)\\n- **State Cache**: `state/cache.go` holds in-memory alert state for fast access\\n- **State Persistence**: Multiple persister implementations:\\n  - `state/persister_sync.go` - Synchronous write to database\\n  - `state/persister_sync_rule.go` - Sync at rule group level\\n  - `state/persister_async.go` - Asynchronous batched writes\\n  - `state/persister_async_rule.go` - Async at rule group level\\n- **Instance Store Interface**: Multiple implementations for reading/writing instance state\\n  - `state/multi_instance_reader.go` - Reads from multiple backends during feature flag transitions\\n  - `state/store_state_reader.go` - Reads state from database (for HA mode)\\n\\n## 5. History Writer (`state/historian/` and `writer/`)\\n\\nThe history writer subsystem records all alert state transitions for audit trails and panel annotations. Implemented in:\\n\\n- **Historian Core**: `state/historian/core.go` - Logic for determining which transitions to record\\n  - `ShouldRecord()` - Decides if a transition should be written to history\\n  - `ShouldRecordAnnotation()` - Decides if dashboard annotations should be created\\n  - Label fingerprinting for stable alert identification\\n\\n- **Backend Abstraction**: `state/historian/backend.go` defines `BackendType`:\\n  - `annotations` - Stores in Grafana dashboard annotations\\n  - `loki` - Remote Loki for long-term retention\\n  - `prometheus` - Remote Prometheus for metrics\\n  - `multiple` - Hybrid multi-backend setup\\n  - `noop` - Disabled\\n\\n- **Backend Implementations**:\\n  - `state/historian/annotation.go` / `annotation_store.go` - Grafana annotations backend\\n  - `state/historian/loki.go` - Remote Loki backend\\n  - `state/historian/prometheus.go` - Remote Prometheus backend\\n  - `state/historian/multiple.go` - Multi-backend coordinator\\n\\n- **Remote Writer**: `writer/datasourcewriter.go` - Generic datasource writer for remote backends\\n\\n## 6. Notifier/Alertmanager (`notifier/`)\\n\\nThe notification subsystem manages alert routing and notification delivery:\\n\\n- **MultiOrgAlertmanager**: `notifier/multiorg_alertmanager.go` - Multi-tenant wrapper\\n  - Manages per-organization Alertmanager instances\\n  - Handles configuration loading and synchronization\\n  - Manages clustering peers for HA deployments\\n  - Remote primary/secondary modes for delegated alertmanaging\\n\\n- **Alertmanager Interface**: `notifier/alertmanager.go` defines core operations:\\n  - Config management (apply, save, retrieve)\\n  - Silence operations (create, delete, list)\\n  - Alert operations (get, put)\\n  - Receiver management\\n  - Status tracking\\n\\n- **Configuration**: `notifier/alertmanager_config.go` - Alertmanager configuration handling\\n- **Auto-generation**: `notifier/autogen_alertmanager.go` - Default config generation\\n- **Receivers**: `notifier/receiver_svc.go` - Receiver CRUD operations\\n- **Silences**: `notifier/silence_svc.go` - Silence management\\n- **Sender**: `notifier/sender.go` - Alert sending to Alertmanager\\n\\n## 7. Alerts Router/Sender (`sender/`)\\n\\nResponsible for routing evaluated alerts to the Alertmanager:\\n\\n- **AlertsRouter**: `sender/router.go` - Main router that syncs config and routes alerts\\n  - Loads Alertmanager configuration from database\\n  - Applies configuration to Alertmanager instances\\n  - Periodically polls configuration for changes\\n  - Dispatches alerts to appropriate Alertmanager\\n\\n- **External Alertmanager Sender**: `sender/sender.go` - Sends alerts to external Alertmanagers\\n  - Queue-based alert batching\\n  - HTTP client management\\n  - Retry and backoff logic\\n\\n- **Notifier**: `sender/notifier.go` - Adapts alerts for Alertmanager format\\n\\n## 8. Evaluation (`eval/`)\\n\\nRule evaluation engine in `pkg/services/ngalert/eval/`:\\n\\n- **Evaluator**: `eval/eval.go` - Executes alert rule queries\\n  - Supports queries against Prometheus-compatible datasources\\n  - Supports Grafana expressions (math, reduce, etc.)\\n  - Returns numeric values with labels\\n  - Handles no-data and error conditions\\n\\n- **EvaluatorFactory**: Creates evaluators with proper dependencies\\n- **Validation**: `eval/validate.go` - Validates rule conditions before execution\\n- **Context**: `eval/context.go` - Execution context for evaluations\\n\\n## 9. Evaluation Runner\\n\\nThe `evaluationRunner` in `evaluation_runner.go` coordinates the evaluation pipeline:\\n\\n- Spawns goroutines for each rule evaluation\\n- Calls the scheduler to get rules\\n- Invokes evaluators\\n- Passes results to state manager\\n- Handles lifecycle (startup, shutdown)\\n\\n## Data Flow\\n\\n1. **Startup**: `ngalert.go:init()` initializes all components, warming up state cache from database\\n2. **Scheduling**: Scheduler fetches rules from store and builds evaluation schedule\\n3. **Evaluation**: EvaluationRunner triggers rule evaluations at scheduled intervals\\n4. **State Management**: Evaluator results flow to State Manager which:\\n   - Compares against previous state\\n   - Generates StateTransition objects\\n   - Calls StatePersister to save state\\n   - Calls Historian to record changes\\n5. **Notification**: State transitions are sent to AlertsRouter which:\\n   - Formats alerts\\n   - Routes to Alertmanager\\n   - Alertmanager applies routing and sending rules\\n6. **Persistence**: History Writer backends persist state transitions for audit/dashboards\\n\\n## Key Interfaces\\n\\n- `AlertingStore` / `RuleStore` - Store layer contracts\\n- `ScheduleService` - Scheduler contract\\n- `AlertInstanceManager` - State access\\n- `Historian` - History writing\\n- `Alertmanager` - Notification interface\\n- `StatePersister` - State persistence\\n- `EvaluatorFactory` - Rule evaluation\\n\\nThis architecture enables Grafana to evaluate alert rules at scale with support for HA deployments, multiple notification backends, and comprehensive state history tracking.\"\n}\n",
